{"nick":"joepie91","message":"vulpix1337: the key point here is: things like apostrophes, stuff that looks like HTML tags, etc. are *valid data* in and of themselves, and should be stored exactly as supplied by the user; only when they are used in a context where that 'special data' has a meaning different from its literal meaning, do you need to do anything with it (which is why you escape output, not input)","date":"2018-12-12T16:16:17.337Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"especially since the same data may be used in different contexts, where different things have special meaning","date":"2018-12-12T16:16:31.471Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"<strong>foo</strong> has a special meaning in HTML, but not in JSON","date":"2018-12-12T16:16:46.604Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"so you escape the < and > if you're displaying that value in a HTML context, but not in a JSON context; which means you can't do anything to the value on *input*, because you don't yet know how it's going to be used in the future","date":"2018-12-12T16:17:22.684Z","type":"message"}
